The price is fair.&lt;br /&gt;The battery capacity is excellent. Have used a half dozen times without need for recharging. Cordless feature is great to trim in shower and not make a mess in bathroom.&lt;br /&gt;The bells and whistles such as turbo power and vacuum chamber are more annoying than useful. The vacuum chamber fills really fast and if you have black hair you can not distinguish it against the groomer&#x27;s black body color despite what the advertisements claim. When the chamber is full cutting ability drops dramatically. The work around is just pull off or keep open the chamber door while grooming.&lt;br /&gt;I have not figured out what turbo is for, sure the blades move faster and the device is louder but since we&#x27;re triming hair and not a full lawn of grass it seems pretty pointless.&lt;br /&gt;The power button is very sensitive and an inadvertant flick of a finger easily shuts off (or turns on trimmer). Not a disaster but slightly annoying.&lt;br /&gt;As far as reliability it has lasted longer than my previous Panasonic so that&#x27;s a plus.</li>

    <li> Purchased the T980 trimmer in January (is now mid-Oct), and it has worked well. Unit shipped with a decent (not great) flip-cover travel case, large enough for the trimmer &amp; charger, and with a small net pouch for the narrow trimming head (which has not been used). Have also never needed the \\&quot;Turbo\\&quot; mode.  The \\&quot;vacuum\\&quot; feature on the T980 works somewhat better than the earlier unit: it does not catch everything, but certainly captures most of the clippings. The flip open door to empty the contents is convenient.  Don&#x27;t care for the hard body, but there is a nice rubber ring (used to change the cutting depth) that makes a good grip point. Find it difficult to read the \\&quot;zoom\\&quot; - that is, cutting depth - setting from certain angles / lighting conditions, but this is not a major problem.  After some 9 months of use, this unit still looks great, cuts great, and has a pleasingly long battery life. It lacks a multi-LED charge indicator, but does have a \\&quot;Low\\&quot; battery warning light (+ a Charge light) &amp; the unit will still run for several beard trimmings once the warning light comes on. All-in-all, a good purchase.</li>

    <li> Until recently, I had been using a Remington beard trimmer I had received as a Christmas gift from about 5 years ago. The shaver comes with 9 different preset trimming sizes so there is plenty of room for dynamic trimming. The flexible trim guard was something I immediately noticed and enjoyed, since my previous trimmer did not have this feature. In addition the flexibility really does allow you to get a precision trim really easily as it contours to the face great.    The T980 comes with a 2 bristle (one soft, one hard) brush for cleaning out the clippers but what really is unique about this trimmer is the vacuum that is attached to it. The vacuum is made so that there is less of a clean up once your done trimming your beard, although it doesn&#x27;t catch all the trimmings it did catch most of them and clean up was much faster than what I am used too. It also comes with a smaller clipper attachment for precision sculpting or just your run of the mill mustache trimming which is slid on and off with ease.    The shaver also comes with a Turbo Mode but the only thing this really does that I have noticed is give the vacuum more power, it may also speed up the clippers but I am not sure about that it seems to clip nicely whether the Turbo Mode is on or off. I think because of the vacuum this trimmer seems a bit louder during operation than my last trimmer but by no means is it a chainsaw (haha).    Finally, the trimmer comes with a travel bag for easy storage on trips which I thought was thoughtful. The only qualm I had was the packaging...it comes in a really sturdy clam shell package and with no helpful opening tabs so it could take you at least a few minutes to get everything out without cutting yourself on sharp plastic edges but since that has nothing to do with the performance of the trimmer I wont go on about that.    So all in all, this trimmer is a fine replacement; dare I say upgrade to my last trimmer, it is said, \\&quot;You get what you pay for\\&quot; well, with the Norelco T980 I think you may be getting that and then some! Precision trimming, ease of use, and convenient clean up and features makes this shaver a must buy for any man especially those on the job hunt!</li>

    <li> I must say that I disagree with most reviewers on this product.  I have several problems with the design which I would like to share.      First, a disclaimer.  The product title says that it is a hair \\&quot;trimmer\\&quot; and not a \\&quot;clipper\\&quot;.  Perhaps I did not see the distinction at first, but I see that others purchase this unit as a clipper as well.  So, as a trimmer (used very frequently and with very short hair trimmings) this unit may work for you.  But even as a trimmer, if the hair is cut at any length (and there are 9 settings to the guide), this thing is useless.    First, the \\&quot;on\\&quot; and \\&quot;turbo\\&quot; buttons are too easy to push while handling, and I&#x27;m constantly startling myself with the turbo setting (it is a little loud).  Also, I find that the guide/vacuum design is poor.  This may work OK if you are trimming short guide settings, but if you get a clump of hair in the guide, which happens constantly with me, it will block the tiny opening for the hair cup.  The vacuum is not strong enough to pull the hair in, and it clogs the whole works.  If you do not notice this, the blockage will prevent the trimmer from trimming, and you may think that a lower guide setting is needed.  You can see how this sets you up for a scalp job when the low guide setting is finally low enough to make a cut.  I just find the whole set up \\&quot;gimmicky\\&quot; and I will take the old standard guides and no vacuum any day.    It does have a strong battery and if you are just lightly trimming a mustache or a beard, it may be the right choice for you.  I think people like me would not be disappointed (and would not have purchased the product) if it had been called the Philips Norelco T980 Turbo Beard and Mustache Vacuum Trimmer.  Long title, but descriptive enough to avoid purchasing the wrong product.</li>

This suffering will take down its operating ability and cause the charge to last less each time you use it.    I&#x27;ve trained my battery correctly from the start (turn it on and leave it to expend itself when I opened the box and then give it the first good, solid nights charge).     <li> This is my first beard trimmer for use with my first beard.  I read many of the other reviews of the Norelco T980 and having a Norelco electric razor decided to give it a try.  I&#x27;ve been generally impressed, although I&#x27;ve never owned another trimmer to compare the T980 to.    Some of the concerns that others noted (followed by my own impressions):  Loudness:  Yes, trimming with a mini-vacuum is a little louder than without.  In particular, when &#x27;Turbo&#x27; mode is on, it sounds like a mini-buzz-saw.  That said, unless you&#x27;re worried about waking a sleeping baby in the same room, it&#x27;s not obnoxiously loud.    Vacuum doesn&#x27;t catch clippings:  Even though this is my first beard, I know trimmings tend to go everywhere when trimming a beard.  I didn&#x27;t expect the vacuum to catch everything (especially since I&#x27;m using the trimmer to leave my beard at a 1/2\\&quot; length- setting 7 of 9).  I always use &#x27;Turbo&#x27; mode (hoping that more suction will catch more of the clippings), and I tend to catch ~75% of the clippings this way.  The biggest issue is that the clippings it doesn&#x27;t catch tend to be the ones that go sailing across the room (for my wife to find later)-but I would assume any trimmer would do that with my facial hair.     Needs frequent charging:  As I said above, I always use the trimmer in &#x27;Turbo&#x27; mode and it&#x27;s not supposed to last very long that way.  However, I&#x27;ve been using three times a week for the last month and have charged it twice.  Charging once every couple of weeks was within my expectations.    Smaller trimmer involves removing regular trim head:  People who complained about having to change trim heads must be in a much more significant hurry than I am in the morning.  The height guide and standard trim head slip off easily (5 seconds or less-literally).  The precision trim head slips on just as easily and really does a nice job with touch-up areas.  The precision trim head extends away from the body of the trimmer more than the standard one, making it easier to clean up errant hair.    Height guide slips when trimming:  I haven&#x27;t seen this problem at all.  I was very concerned about it (I didn&#x27;t want to accidentally shave off the beard I spent all this time growing), but really, any concern of this at all can be eliminated by holding the trimmer so that your grip doesn&#x27;t allow the height guide to move (which, at least for me, is a perfectly normal way to hold the trimmer).    The storage pouch is a little weird, but I found I can fit both the trimmer and my electric razor in it without any problems, so all the better.    Bottom line- the T980 is generally a good little trimmer.</li>

UPDATE: I called Norelco before the 2-year warrantee elapsed. Since the whisker tray broke in two pieces and the spring-loaded beard guide is on it&#x27;s last leg (thin plastic holds in the \\&quot;springs\\&quot; and is very fragile), Norelco decided to replace the unit en toto. They said they&#x27;d send a new one out and that I should just put the old one back in the same box, apply the PP label they&#x27;ll include and drop the whole enchilada in the mail. It&#x27;s nearly two weeks, and I still haven&#x27;t seen hide nor hair of the new shaver. Only time will tell if Norelco stands behind their product (and their promises).    UPDATE (3/11/09): Well, the replacement unit finally came, after three weeks and four phone callls. Apparently, the thing was on backorder, but nobody at Phillips/Norelco Customer Service bothered to disclose that fact, nor did they provide a tracking number. After my fourth call yesterday, they finally provided me a UPS tracking number which was moot as the package arrived when I returned home from work. So far, so good..at least it works and isn&#x27;t falling apart. Unfortunately, I have no faith that this one will perform and hold-up any better than the first. At least I won&#x27;t have to buy another until this one breaks.    Update (7/22/09): Well, only four months after receiving the new replacement trimmer, the whisker tray (aka \\&quot;hair collection chamber\\&quot;) has fallen apart, just like it did on my original defective trimmer. The difference this time is that Norelco is hanging me out to dry and is refusing to do anything to repair/replace this poorly designed and manufactured product. They claim that because the warantee period is up on the ORIGINAL defective unit, that they can do nothing about the replacement unit they supplied, i.e., they won&#x27;t stand behind the product even though any other new one has a TWO-Year warrantee. FYI, the original unit was bought from Amazon on 4/7/07. As such, I am downgrading the original 3-star rating to ONE-STAR and changing my review title from \\&quot;It&#x27;s Just OK\\&quot; to reflect my true feelings about this product. As such, I will NEVER buy another Phillips-Norelco product again!</li>

I haven&#x27;t found the \\&quot;turbo\\&quot; mode to be that helpful. From my perspective, it seems to be a marketing tool designed to convince guys that they&#x27;re getting a really powerful, studly shaver. Power in a car, I can understand. But in a trimmer? Anyway, this is a great little trimmer. I just question the degree to which the new features are improvements.</li>

    <li> Design flaw #1:&lt;br /&gt;The \\&quot;lockable\\&quot; length settings don&#x27;t lock. So if you apply a normal amount of pressure to the device, your number 5 beard setting will be pushed down to a number 1. They should&#x27;ve built some sort of locking switch onto this thing.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Design flaw #2:&lt;br /&gt;When you remove the trimmer guard to just use the trimming blade itself for detail trimming, the blue plastic vacuum guard blocks the trimming blade. You have to push it against your hair line for the plastic guard to move out of the way. Trying to catch the hair is good, but this is not a good design for precise trimming.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Design flaw #3:&lt;br /&gt;They give you an additional smaller trimming blade for detail work on the moustache, but it isn&#x27;t built into the trimmer, so you have to remove the outer guard, remove the inner trimming blade, usually clean out all the hair, then attach the new trimming blade. My old trimmer had a switch that just caused a smaller trimmer blade to pop out, so I didn&#x27;t have to remove all of the other stuff this trimmer makes you remove. That would&#x27;ve been a better design.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Design flaw #4:&lt;br /&gt;The on switch is just a big button you press down on and not a switch. So if you want to stick this in the supplied travel bag and into your suitcase, expect it to accidentally turn on. You can also accidentally turn it off while shaving if you don&#x27;t watch your grip. A better design would&#x27;ve been a switch.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Design flaw #5:&lt;br /&gt;Since it&#x27;s a vacuum, it has a hair reservoir. They did one good thing this time and actually made the beard reservoir window clear. But it&#x27;s not removable and it&#x27;s just a door that opens up - so it&#x27;s harder to clean out. Also, the hair reservoir isn&#x27;t big enough and if you have a moderate or heavy beard, you&#x27;ll find yourself cleaning this trimmer out every time you use it (which is what it recommends in the manual). Who has time for that?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The vacuum doesn&#x27;t catch enough hair for it to be worth all of the inconveniences of its design flaws. Maybe one day they can get this design right. Until then, save your money and use a regular shaver with replaceable trimming attachments and put down a paper towel to catch the hair.s design right.     <li> If we&#x27;re completely honest, we&#x27;ve been conditioned by manufacturers these days to accept rubbish without complaint.  Quite true, you can dial into their computer and navigate circles around their voicemail system for a few hours until your anger dissipates.  Or is transferred to computer answering systems.  Whichever comes first.     Happily, however, such is not the case with the Philips Norelco T980 Turbo Vacuum Trimmer.      Not only does this eager little trimmer solve several problems at once but it does so with a composure and aplomb that will sweep away the corporate fog and, suddenly, everything else you own will seem completely and utterly inadequate.    Trimming whiskers used to be such a chore that the ZZ Top look began to show some sense, if not appeal.  The constant recharging, sweeping up afterward, seemingly endless search for single-tasking components that had wandered off and an assembly/disassembly process for cleaning the tool that would make Bill Gates weep.  Philips, however, decided to go in a slightly different direction.    For a start, the battery holds on to a charge with a grip that would make Chuck Liddell cry. It doesn&#x27;t last mere hours, days or weeks.  Under standard use, mine lasts well over a month.  Even when the battery light does begin to blink, what it really means to say is, \\&quot;Pardon me but, at some point in the next several days, when it isn&#x27;t too much of a bother, could you please plug me in for a bit?\\&quot;  Nothing urgent about it whatsoever.  And once the lead is connected from socket to trimmer, a scant hour will have it fully refreshed and ready for another month on the road.    Then there is the all-in-one design.  Unlike most trimmers, which require that you dig around to find the correct attachment in order to trim your left eyebrow now that you&#x27;re done with the right, nearly everything is built directly into this sleek little unit.  The only exception is a neat little detail trimmer that stands eternally at the ready in itsown clear and obvious pocket inside the travel pouch.  That&#x27;s it.  Nothing else to search out when you&#x27;re dashing to work.  It&#x27;s all right there.    Not everyone who sells a \\&quot;vacuum trimmer\\&quot; truly means it.  Most generate just a bit of wind, sufficient to scatter your whiskers over the widest possible surface.  I firmly believe my last vacuum trimmer was designed by a consortium of housekeepers seeking job security.  The T980, however, actually captures every single whisker, every single time.  And then there&#x27;s a Turbo button that doubles the already adequate force of the vacuum&#x27;s suction so that you can give yourself that wind-blown look if you so choose.    But, by far, my favorite thing about this trimmer is the way it feels.  It sits in your hand as if it were custom designed specifically for you.  It&#x27;s lightweight and nimble around the bends, falls effortlessly into its case when deeds are done and assembles as if there is an invisible force guiding your hand at every step of the way.  I am genuinely amazed at the simplicity of removing and replacing the grille guard.  For a time, I thought it must be drawn together by magnets.  But it isn&#x27;t.  It&#x27;s just a set of exceptionally well designed tabs and slots that quickly correct a hurried approach and seat the grille home with a satisfying, subtle click.      Most products on the market today are slapdash clumps of flimsy plastics and mechanics that are carefully designed to fail at the worst possible time.  And, for some reason, we have accepted this corporate abuse in the hopes that prices would compensate us somehow.  But they don&#x27;t really, do they?  When you&#x27;ve re-purchased the same device five times because it keeps breaking, whose interests are truly being served?    So, then, the T980 is a warning shot fired over the bow of companies everywhere who treat their clients like stupid, slobbering monkeys, devoid of choice or rights.  With it, Philips is saying, \\&quot;See, everyone?  You needn&#x27;t accept rubbish in exchange for your hard-earned money.  We&#x27;ve done it properly and at a price point that is competitive.\\&quot;  And why wouldn&#x27;t we honor that?    I wish my hair grew faster.</li>
    <li> I&#x27;ve owned this quite a few years now, and it&#x27;s still going on the original battery. It does a good job of collecting the trimmings, but it won&#x27;t capture 100%. I typically charge it while I am in the shower and then remove the charger to trim (it holds charge very well). Having a wireless trimmer makes it easier to maneuver.  Shaving while plugged in often makes it slightly more difficult to use.  Overall, this is a great product, granted I&#x27;ve only used it a limited number of times.  My suggestion, if you&#x27;re neurotic about trim length, is to look around and find a trimmer with trimming attachments for varying lengths because of the occasional twist of the zoom feature that changes the trimming length.</li>

    <li> A beard trimmer with a built-in vacuum to keep the trimmings from collecting all over your sink is a good thing. The nicad battery life is acceptable -- I get a week of trims on my full beard and moustache at the Turbo setting. I will be interested to see how well the blades hold up to the \\&quot;ever-sharp\\&quot; claim.  No lubrication needed either!  I am deducting one star because of failings in the instructions and packaging.  The instructions never tell you which side of the trimmer to hold against your face, and the T980 works the opposite of most other trimmers and shavers.  Most others have you hold the side with the buttons and logo against your face; when you use the length comb on the T980, however,you hold it with the buttons and logo on the side facing AWAY from your face.  I wonder how many of my fellow reviewers have been using this trimmer correctly, given this unconventional orientation.  Nowhere in the instructions do they show a clear photo of a guy using the trimmer.  There are two tiny, hard-to-follow line illustrations.  Adding insult to injury, the first time I called Norelco for help, the woman rep on the phone -- adding helpfully that she had never used a beard trimmer herself -- gave me the wrong answer.  Further experimentation -- and another call to a male rep -- confirmed that I was using the trimmer correctly.  The other problem with the packaging is the dreadful plastic blister pack holding the trimmer and accessories inside the box.  Any package requiring scissors to open needs to be redesigned with more eco- and user-friendly materials!!!  At any rate, the T980 is the current state-of-the-art in vacuum beard trimmers, and I recommend it, the packaging notwithstanding.e woman rep on the phone -- adding helpfully that she had never used a beard trimmer herself -- gave me the wrong answer.
